          <span class="mw-tmh-playtext">
           Play media
          </span>
         </span>
        </a>
       </div>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Master_Mystery_(trailer)_-_Burton_King_-_1919,_B.A._Rolfe_Photoplays_-_EYE_FLM41533_-_OB_685697.webm" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Silent movie
        <i>
         The Master Mystery
        </i>
        (1919). Running time: 09:39. Episode of a serial in fifteen episodes with magician and escape artist Houdini in the lead.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1906 Houdini started showing films of his outside escapes as part of his vaudeville act. In Boston he presented a short film called
      <i>
       Houdini Defeats Hackenschmidt
      </i>
      .
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georg_Hackenschmidt" title="Georg Hackenschmidt">
       Georg Hackenschmidt
      </a>
      was a famous wrestler of the day, but the nature of their contest is unknown as the film is lost.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1909 Houdini made a film in Paris for Cinema Lux titled
      <i>
       Merveilleux Exploits du Clbre Houdini  Paris
      </i>
      (Marvellous Exploits of the Famous Houdini in Paris).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It featured a loose narrative designed to showcase several of Houdini's famous escapes, including his straitjacket and underwater handcuff escapes. That same year Houdini got an offer to star as
      <a href="/wiki/Captain_Nemo" title="Captain Nemo">
       Captain Nemo
      </a>
      in a silent version of
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/20,000_Leagues_Under_the_Sea" title="20,000 Leagues Under the Sea">
        20,000 Leagues Under the Sea
       </a>
      </i>
      , but the project never made it into production.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is often erroneously reported that Houdini served as special-effects consultant on the Wharton/International cliffhanger serial,
      <i>
       The Mysteries of Myra
      </i>
      , shot in Ithaca, New York, because Harry Grossman, director of
      <i>
       The Master Mystery
      </i>
      also filmed a serial in Ithaca at about the same time. The consultants on the serial were pioneering
      <a href="/wiki/Hereward_Carrington" title="Hereward Carrington">
       Hereward Carrington
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Aleister_Crowley" title="Aleister Crowley">
       Aleister Crowley
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1918 Houdini signed a contract with film producer
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B.A._Rolfe" title="B.A. Rolfe">
       B.A. Rolfe
      </a>
      to star in a 15-part
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serial_(film)" title="Serial (film)">
       serial
      </a>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Master_Mystery" title="The Master Mystery">
        The Master Mystery
       </a>
      </i>
      (released in January 1919). As was common at the time, the film serial was released simultaneously with a novel. Financial difficulties resulted in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolfe_Photoplays_Inc." title="Rolfe Photoplays Inc.">
       B.A. Rolfe Productions
      </a>
      going out of business, but
      <i>
       The Master Mystery
      </i>
      led to Houdini being signed by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Famous_Players-Lasky_Corporation" title="Famous Players-Lasky Corporation">
       Famous Players-Lasky Corporation
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">
       Paramount Pictures
      </a>
      , for whom he made two pictures,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Grim_Game" title="The Grim Game">
        The Grim Game
       </a>
      </i>
      (1919) and
      <i>
       Terror Island
      </i>
      (1920).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Grim_Game" title="The Grim Game">
        The Grim Game
       </a>
      </i>
      was Houdini's first full-length movie and is reputed to be his best. Because of the inflammable nature of nitrate film only 10 percent of old silent movies exist. Film historians considered the film lost. One copy did exist hidden in the collection of a private collector only known to a tiny group magicians that saw it. Dick Brookz and Dorothy Dietrich of The Houdini Museum in
      <a href="/wiki/Scranton,_Pennsylvania" title="Scranton, Pennsylvania">
       Scranton, Pennsylvania
      </a>
      had seen it twice on the invitation of the collector. After many years of trying, they finally got him to agree to sell the film to
      <a href="/wiki/Turner_Classic_Movies" title="Turner Classic Movies">
       Turner Classic Movies
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      who have restored the complete 71-minute film. The film, not seen by the general public for 96 years will be shown by TCM on March 29, 2015 as a highlight of their yearly 4-day festival in Hollywood. Dorothy Dietrich and Dick Brookz are being brought out to Hollywood to introduce the film.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The collector died in October 2014, soon after the sale. The film is then scheduled to be shown at The Directors Guild in NYC and then in Scranton, PA. the home of the Houdini Museum, after which Turner Classic Movies will show it on their network.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Houdini_swims_river_in_scene_from_The_man_from_beyond_(cropped).JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="455" data-file-width="311" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Houdini_swims_river_in_scene_from_The_man_from_beyond_%28cropped%29.JPG/170px-Houdini_swims_river_in_scene_from_The_man_from_beyond_%28cropped%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Houdini_swims_river_in_scene_from_The_man_from_beyond_%28cropped%29.JPG/255px-Houdini_swims_river_in_scene_from_The_man_from_beyond_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/52/Houdini_swims_river_in_scene_from_The_man_from_beyond_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Houdini_swims_river_in_scene_from_The_man_from_beyond_(cropped).JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Houdini swims above
        <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls" title="Niagara Falls">
         Niagara Falls
        </a>
        in a scene from
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/The_Man_from_Beyond" title="The Man from Beyond">
          The Man from Beyond
         </a>
        </i>
        (1922)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      While filming an aerial stunt for
      <i>
       The Grim Game
      </i>
      , two biplanes collided in mid-air with a stuntman doubling Houdini dangling by a rope from one of the planes. Publicity was geared heavily toward promoting this dramatic "caught on film" moment, claiming it was Houdini himself dangling from the plane. While filming these movies in Los Angeles, Houdini rented a home in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laurel_Canyon,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Laurel Canyon, Los Angeles, California">
       Laurel Canyon
      </a>
      . Following his two-picture stint in Hollywood, Houdini returned to New York and started his own film production company called the "Houdini Picture Corporation". He produced and starred in two films,
      <i>
       The Man From Beyond
      </i>
      (1921) and
      <i>
       Haldane of the Secret Service
      </i>
      (1923). He also founded his own film laboratory business called The Film Development Corporation (FDC), gambling on a new process for developing motion picture film. Houdini's brother,
      <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Hardeen" title="Theodore Hardeen">
       Theodore Hardeen
      </a>
      , left his own career as a magician and escape artist to run the company. Magician
      <a href="/wiki/Harry_Kellar" title="Harry Kellar">
       Harry Kellar
      </a>
      was a major investor.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Neither Houdini's acting career nor FDC found success, and he gave up on the movie business in 1923, complaining that "the profits are too meager".
     </p>
     <p>
      In April 2008, Kino International released a DVD box set of Houdini's surviving silent films, including
      <i>
       The Master Mystery
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Terror Island
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       The Man From Beyond
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Haldane of the Secret Service
      </i>
      , and five minutes from
      <i>
       The Grim Game
      </i>
      . The set also includes newsreel footage of Houdini's escapes from 1907 to 1923, and a section from
      <i>
       Merveilleux Exploits du Clbre Houdini  Paris,
      </i>
      although it is not identified as such.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Aviator">
       Aviator
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      In 1909, Houdini became fascinated with aviation. He purchased a French
      <a href="/wiki/Voisin_1907_biplane" title="Voisin 1907 biplane">
       Voisin biplane
      </a>
      for $5000 and hired a full-time mechanic, Antonio Brassac. After crashing once, he made his first successful flight on November 26 in
      <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">
       Hamburg
      </a>
      , Germany. The following year, Houdini toured Australia. He brought along his Voisin biplane with the intention to be the first person in Australia to fly.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Falsely_reported_as_pioneer">
       Falsely reported as pioneer
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On March 18, 1910, he made three flights at
      <a href="/wiki/Diggers_Rest,_Victoria" title="Diggers Rest, Victoria">
       Diggers Rest, Victoria
      </a>
      , near Melbourne. It was reported at the time that this was the first aerial flight in Australia,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smh_48-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-smh-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a century later, some major news outlets still credit him with this feat.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Wing Commander
      <a href="/wiki/Harry_Cobby" title="Harry Cobby">
       Harry Cobby
      </a>
      wrote in
      <i>
       Aircraft
      </i>
      in March 1938 that "the first aeroplane flight in the Southern Hemisphere was made on December 9, 1909 by Mr
      <a href="/wiki/Colin_Defries" title="Colin Defries">
       Colin Defries
      </a>
      , a Londoner, at
      <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Park_Racecourse,_Sydney" title="Victoria Park Racecourse, Sydney">
       Victoria Park Racecourse, Sydney
      </a>
      , in a Wilbur Wright aeroplane".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Colin Defries was a trained pilot, having learnt to fly in Cannes, France. By modern standards his flight time was minimal, but in 1909 he had accumulated enough to become an instructor. On his first flight he took off, maintained straight and level flight, albeit briefly, and landed safely. His crash landing on his second flight, when he tried to retrieve his hat which was blown off, demonstrated what a momentary lack of attention could cause while flying a
      <a href="/wiki/Wright_Model_A" title="Wright Model A">
       Wright Model A
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      It is accepted by Australian historians
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the Aviation Historical Society of Australia that the definition of flight established by the Gorell Committee on behalf of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aero_Club_of_Great_Britain" title="Aero Club of Great Britain">
       Aero Club of Great Britain
      </a>
      dictates the acceptance of a flight or its rejection, giving Colin Defries credit as the first to make an aeroplane flight in Australia, and the Southern Hemisphere.
     </p>
     <p>
      Additionally, aviation pioneer
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Pearse" title="Richard Pearse">
       Richard Pearse
      </a>
      is believed by many New Zealand historians to have undertaken his first flight as early as 1902, which would give him not only the Southern Hemisphere but the World record, although this is disputed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1965 aviation journalist
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stanley_Brogden" title="Stanley Brogden">
       Stanley Brogden
      </a>
      formed the view that the first powered flight in Australia took place at Bolivar in South Australia; the aircraft was a Bleriot monoplane with Fred Custance as the pilot. The flight took place on March 17, 1910. The next day when Houdini took to the air, the Herald newspaper reported Custance's flight, stating it had lasted 5minutes 25seconds at a height of between 12 and 15feet.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smh_48-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-smh-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2010
      <a href="/wiki/Australia_Post" title="Australia Post">
       Australia Post
      </a>
      issued stamps commemorating Colin Defries, Houdini and
      <a href="/wiki/John_Robertson_Duigan" title="John Robertson Duigan">
       John Robertson Duigan
      </a>
      , crediting only Defries and Duigan with historical firsts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Duigan was an Australian pioneer aviator who built and flew the
      <a href="/wiki/Duigan_pusher_biplane" title="Duigan pusher biplane">
       first Australian-made aircraft
      </a>
      . Australia Post did acknowledge the part Houdini played (
      <i>
       Harry Houdini can't escape being part of Australia's history
      </i>
      ) but did not attribute any record to him.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="After_Australia">
       After Australia
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      After completing his Australia tour, Houdini put the Voisin into storage in England. He announced he would use it to fly from city to city during his next Music Hall tour, and even promised to leap from it handcuffed, but he never flew again.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Debunking_spiritualists">
       Debunking spiritualists
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Houdini_and_Lincoln.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="722" data-file-width="752" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Houdini_and_Lincoln.jpg/220px-Houdini_and_Lincoln.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Houdini_and_Lincoln.jpg/330px-Houdini_and_Lincoln.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Houdini_and_Lincoln.jpg/440px-Houdini_and_Lincoln.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Houdini_and_Lincoln.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Houdini demonstrates how a
        <a href="/wiki/Photographer" title="Photographer">
         photographer
        </a>
        could produce fraudulent "spirit photographs" that documented the apparition and social interaction of the dead
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
         <a href="#cite_note-57">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          57
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the 1920s Houdini turned his energies toward debunking
      <a href="/wiki/Parapsychology" title="Parapsychology">
       psychics
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Mediumship" title="Mediumship">
       mediums
      </a>
      , a pursuit that inspired and was followed by latter-day
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stage_magician" title="Stage magician">
       stage magicians
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conjure_58-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Conjure-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Houdini's training in magic allowed him to expose frauds who had successfully fooled many scientists and academics. He was a member of a
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Scientific_American" title="Scientific American">
        Scientific American
       </a>
      </i>
      committee that offered a cash prize to any medium who could successfully demonstrate
      <a href="/wiki/Supernatural" title="Supernatural">
       supernatural
      </a>
      abilities. None was able to do so, and the prize was never collected. The first to be tested was medium George Valentine of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilkes_Barre,_Pennsylvania" title="Wilkes Barre, Pennsylvania">
       Wilkes Barre, Pennsylvania
      </a>
      . As his fame as a "ghostbuster" grew, Houdini took to attending
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9ance" title="Sance">
       sances
      </a>
      in disguise, accompanied by a reporter and police officer. Possibly the most famous medium whom he debunked was
      <a href="/wiki/Mina_Crandon" title="Mina Crandon">
       Mina Crandon
      </a>
      , also known as "Margery".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "Houdini exposed numerous phony mediums and inspired other magicians to follow suit. The Amazing Randi, (Dorothy) Dietrich, Penn &amp; Teller and Dick Brookz are magicians that have exposed these unscrupulous mediums."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_60-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Williams-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Houdini chronicled his debunking exploits in his book,
      <i>
       A Magician Among the Spirits
      </i>
      , co-authored with
      <a href="/wiki/C._M._Eddy,_Jr." title="C. M. Eddy, Jr.">
       C. M. Eddy, Jr.
      </a>
      , who was not credited. These activities cost Houdini the friendship of Sir
      <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Conan_Doyle" title="Arthur Conan Doyle">
       Arthur Conan Doyle
      </a>
      . Doyle, a firm believer in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spiritualism_(religious_movement)" title="Spiritualism (religious movement)">
       spiritualism
      </a>
      during his later years, refused to believe any of Houdini's exposs. Doyle came to believe that Houdini was a powerful spiritualist medium, and had performed many of his stunts by means of paranormal abilities and was using these abilities to block those of other mediums that he was "debunking".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This disagreement led to the two men becoming public antagonists and led Sir Arthur to view Houdini as a dangerous enemy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simon_.26_Schuster_18-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Simon_.26_Schuster-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Before Houdini died, he and his wife agreed that if Houdini found it possible to communicate after death, he would communicate the message "Rosabelle believe", a secret code which they agreed to use. Rosabelle was their favorite song. Bess held yearly
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seances" title="Seances">
       sances
      </a>
      on
      <a href="/wiki/Halloween" title="Halloween">
       Halloween
      </a>
      for ten years after Houdini's death. She did claim to have contact through
      <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Ford_(psychic)" title="Arthur Ford (psychic)">
       Arthur Ford
      </a>
      in 1929 when Ford conveyed the secret code, but Bess later said the incident had been faked.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simon_.26_Schuster_18-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Simon_.26_Schuster-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The code seems to have been such that it could be broken by Ford or his associates using existing clues.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Evidence to this effect was discovered by Ford's biographer after he died in 1971.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1936, after a last unsuccessful sance on the roof of the
      <a href="/wiki/Knickerbocker_Hotel_(Los_Angeles)" title="Knickerbocker Hotel (Los Angeles)">
       Knickerbocker Hotel
      </a>
      , she put out the candle that she had kept burning beside a photograph of Houdini since his death. In 1943, Bess said that "ten years is long enough to wait for any man."
     </p>
     <p>
      The tradition of holding a sance for Houdini continues, held by magicians throughout the world. The Official Houdini Sance was organized in the 1940s
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Hollis_Radner" title="Sidney Hollis Radner">
       Sidney Hollis Radner
      </a>
      , a Houdini aficionado from Holyoke, Massachusetts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Yearly Houdini sances are also conducted in Chicago at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Excalibur_(nightclub)" title="Excalibur (nightclub)">
       Excalibur
      </a>
      nightclub by "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Necromancer" title="Necromancer">
       necromancer
      </a>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/Neil_Tobin" title="Neil Tobin">
       Neil Tobin
      </a>
      on behalf of the Chicago Assembly of the
      <a href="/wiki/Society_of_American_Magicians" title="Society of American Magicians">
       Society of American Magicians
      </a>
      ;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and at the Houdini Museum in Scranton by magician
      <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Dietrich" title="Dorothy Dietrich">
       Dorothy Dietrich
      </a>
      who previously held them at New York's
      <a href="/wiki/Magic_Towne_House" title="Magic Towne House">
       Magic Towne House
      </a>
      with such magical notables as Houdini biographers
      <a href="/wiki/Walter_B._Gibson" title="Walter B. Gibson">
       Walter B. Gibson
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Milbourne_Christopher" title="Milbourne Christopher">
       Milbourne Christopher
      </a>
      . Gibson was asked by Bess Houdini to carry on the original seance tradition. After doing them for many years at New York's Magic Towne House, before he died, Walter passed on the tradition of conducting of the Original Seances to
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_60-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Williams-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Dietrich" title="Dorothy Dietrich">
       Dorothy Dietrich
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1926, Harry Houdini hired
      <a href="/wiki/H._P._Lovecraft" title="H. P. Lovecraft">
       H. P. Lovecraft
      </a>
      and his friend
      <a href="/wiki/C._M._Eddy,_Jr." title="C. M. Eddy, Jr.">
       C. M. Eddy, Jr.
      </a>
      , to write an entire book about debunking religious miracles, which was to be called
      <i>
       The Cancer of Superstition.
      </i>
      Houdini had earlier asked Lovecraft to write an article about astrology, for which he paid $75. The article does not survive. Lovecraft's detailed synopsis for
      <i>
       Cancer
      </i>
      does survive, as do three chapters of the treatise written by Eddy. Houdini's death derailed the plans, as his widow did not wish to pursue the project.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Appearance_and_voice_recordings">
       Appearance and voice recordings
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jack_Dempsey,_Harry_Houdini_and_Benny_Leonard2.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3911" data-file-width="5460" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Jack_Dempsey%2C_Harry_Houdini_and_Benny_Leonard2.jpg/220px-Jack_Dempsey%2C_Harry_Houdini_and_Benny_Leonard2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Jack_Dempsey%2C_Harry_Houdini_and_Benny_Leonard2.jpg/330px-Jack_Dempsey%2C_Harry_Houdini_and_Benny_Leonard2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Jack_Dempsey%2C_Harry_Houdini_and_Benny_Leonard2.jpg/440px-Jack_Dempsey%2C_Harry_Houdini_and_Benny_Leonard2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jack_Dempsey,_Harry_Houdini_and_Benny_Leonard2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Heavyweight boxer
        <a href="/wiki/Jack_Dempsey" title="Jack Dempsey">
         Jack Dempsey
        </a>
        mock punching Houdini (held back by lightweight boxer
        <a href="/wiki/Benny_Leonard" title="Benny Leonard">
         Benny Leonard
        </a>
        )
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Unlike the image of the classic magician, Houdini was short and stocky and typically appeared on stage in a long frock coat and tie. Most biographers give his height as
      <span class="nowrap">
       5ft 5 in
      </span>
      , but descriptions vary. Houdini was also said to be slightly
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bow-legged" title="Bow-legged">
       bow-legged
      </a>
      , which aided in his ability to gain slack during his rope escapes. In the 1997 biography
      <i>
       Houdini!!!: The Career of Ehrich Weiss
      </i>
      , author
      <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Silverman" title="Kenneth Silverman">
       Kenneth Silverman
      </a>
      summarizes how reporters described Houdini's appearance during his early career:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       They stressed his smallness"somewhat undersized"and angular, vivid features: "He is smooth-shaven with a keen, sharp-chinned, sharp-cheekboned face, bright blue eyes and thick, curly, black hair." Some sensed how much his complexly expressive smile was the outlet of his charismatic stage presence. It communicated to audiences at once warm amiability, pleasure in performing, and, more subtly, imperious self-assurance. Several reporters tried to capture the charming effect, describing him as "happy-looking", "pleasant-faced", "good natured at all times", "the young Hungarian magician with the pleasant smile and easy confidence".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         68
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      Houdini made the only known recordings of his voice on Edison
      <a href="/wiki/Phonograph_cylinder" title="Phonograph cylinder">
       wax cylinders
      </a>
      on October 29, 1914, in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flatbush,_New_York" title="Flatbush, New York">
       Flatbush, New York
      </a>
      . On them, Houdini practices several different introductory speeches for his famous
      <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Water_Torture_Cell" title="Chinese Water Torture Cell">
       Chinese water torture cell
      </a>
      . He also invites his sister, Gladys, to recite a poem. Houdini then recites the same poem in German. The six wax cylinders were discovered in the collection of magician John Mulholland after his death in 1970. They are part of the
      <a href="/wiki/David_Copperfield_(illusionist)" title="David Copperfield (illusionist)">
       David Copperfield
      </a>
      collection.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wild_About_Harry_69-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Wild_About_Harry-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Death">
       Death
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Harry_Houdini_and_his_wife.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="648" height="262" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Harry_Houdini_and_his_wife.jpg/170px-Harry_Houdini_and_his_wife.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Harry_Houdini_and_his_wife.jpg/255px-Harry_Houdini_and_his_wife.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Harry_Houdini_and_his_wife.jpg/340px-Harry_Houdini_and_his_wife.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Harry_Houdini_and_his_wife.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Houdini and his wife
        <a href="/wiki/Bess_Houdini" title="Bess Houdini">
         Bess
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Harry Houdini died of
      <a href="/wiki/Peritonitis" title="Peritonitis">
       peritonitis
      </a>
      , secondary to a
      <a href="/wiki/Appendicitis" title="Appendicitis">
       ruptured appendix
      </a>
      at 1:26p.m. on October 31, 1926 in Room 401 at Detroit's Grace Hospital, aged 52. In his final days, he optimistically held to a strong belief that he would recover, but his last words before dying were reportedly, "I'm tired of fighting."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simon_.26_Schuster_18-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-Simon_.26_Schuster-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Eyewitnesses to an incident at Houdini's dressing room in the Princess Theatre in
      <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
       Montreal
      </a>
      gave rise to speculation that Houdini's death was caused by a
      <a href="/wiki/McGill_University" title="McGill University">
       McGill University
      </a>
      student, J. Gordon Whitehead, who delivered a surprise attack of multiple blows to Houdini's abdomen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snopes_70-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Snopes-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The eyewitnesses, students named Jacques Price and Sam Smilovitz (sometimes called Jack Price and Sam Smiley), proffered accounts of the incident that generally corroborated one another. Price describes Whitehead asking Houdini "if he believed in the miracles of the Bible" and "whether it was true that punches in the stomach did not hurt him". He then delivered "some very hammer-like blows below the belt". Houdini was reclining on a couch at the time, having broken his ankle while performing several days earlier. Price states that Houdini winced at each blow and stopped Whitehead suddenly in the midst of a punch, gesturing that he had had enough, and adding that he had had no opportunity to prepare himself against the blows, as he did not expect Whitehead to strike him so suddenly and forcefully. Had his ankle not been broken, he would have risen from the couch into a better position to brace himself.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snopes_70-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Snopes-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Throughout the evening, Houdini performed in great pain. He was unable to sleep and remained in constant pain for the next two days, but did not seek medical help. When he finally saw a doctor, he was found to have a fever of 102F (39C) and acute appendicitis, and advised to have immediate surgery. He ignored the advice and decided to go on with the show.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_72-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When Houdini arrived at the Garrick Theater in
      <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">
       Detroit
      </a>
      , Michigan, on October 24, 1926, for what would be his last performance, he had a fever of 104F (40C). Despite the diagnosis, Houdini took the stage. He was reported to have passed out during the show, but was revived and continued. Afterwards, he was hospitalized at Detroit's
      <a href="/wiki/Sinai-Grace_Hospital" title="Sinai-Grace Hospital">
       Grace Hospital
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snopes_70-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Snopes-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      It is not entirely clear what relationship the encounter in the dressing room had on Houdini's eventual death.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snopes_70-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Snopes-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snopes" title="Snopes">
       Snopes
      </a>
      points out, the relationship between blunt trauma and appendicitis is not clear. One theory suggests that Houdini was unaware that he was suffering from appendicitis. If he had not realized that his stomach pains were symptomatic of appendicitis, he would not have appreciated the potentially critical effect of the blows to his abdomen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snopes_70-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Snopes-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After taking statements from Price and Smilovitz, Houdini's insurance company concluded that the death was due to the dressing-room incident and paid
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Double_indemnity_(insurance)" title="Double indemnity (insurance)">
       double indemnity
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_72-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Houdini_grave_site">
       Houdini grave site
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Houdini's funeral was held on November 4, 1926 in New York City, with more than 2,000 mourners in attendance.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He was interred in the
      <a href="/wiki/Machpelah_Cemetery_(Queens)" title="Machpelah Cemetery (Queens)">
       Machpelah Cemetery
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Glendale,_Queens" title="Glendale, Queens">
       Glendale, Queens
      </a>
      , with the crest of the
      <a href="/wiki/Society_of_American_Magicians" title="Society of American Magicians">
       Society of American Magicians
      </a>
      inscribed on his grave site. A statuary bust was added to the
      <a href="/wiki/Exedra" title="Exedra">
       exedra
      </a>
      in 1927, a rarity, because graven images are forbidden in Jewish cemeteries. In 1975 the bust was destroyed by vandals. Temporary busts were placed at the grave until 2011 when a group who came to be called The
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Houdini_Commandos&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Houdini Commandos (page does not exist)">
       Houdini Commandos
      </a>
      from the
      <a href="/wiki/Houdini_Museum" title="Houdini Museum">
       Houdini Museum
      </a>
      in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scranton" title="Scranton">
       Scranton
      </a>
      , Pennsylvania placed a permanent bust with the permission of Houdini's family and of the cemetery.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houdini_Returns_75-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Houdini_Returns-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Society_of_American_Magicians" title="Society of American Magicians">
       Society of American Magicians
      </a>
      took responsibility for the upkeep of the site, as Houdini had willed a large sum of money to the organization he had grown from one club to 5,000-6,000 dues-paying membership worldwide. The payment of upkeep was abandoned by the society's dean George Schindler, who said Houdini paid for perpetual care, but theres nobody at the cemetery to provide it, adding that the operator of the cemetery, David Jacobson, sends us a bill for upkeep every year but we never pay it because he never provides any care. The Society tidies the grave themselves.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houdini.27s_Final_Trick_76-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Houdini.27s_Final_Trick-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Machpelah Cemetery operator Jacobson said, they "never paid the cemetery for any restoration of the Houdini family plot in my tenure since 1988," claiming that the money came from the cemetery's dwindling funds. The granite monuments of Houdini's sister, Gladys, and brother, Leopold were also destroyed by vandals.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houdinis.27_Plot_Is_Cleared_Up.2C_and_Then_Thickens_77-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Houdinis.27_Plot_Is_Cleared_Up.2C_and_Then_Thickens-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For many years, until recently, The Houdini grave site has been only cared for by
      <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Dietrich" title="Dorothy Dietrich">
       Dorothy Dietrich
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dick_Brookz" title="Dick Brookz">
       Dick Brookz
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Houdini_Museum" title="Houdini Museum">
       Houdini Museum
      </a>
      in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scranton" title="Scranton">
       Scranton
      </a>
      , Pennsylvania.
     </p>
     <p>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-From_the_President.E2.80.99s_Desk_Dal_Sanders_Page_8_78-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-From_the_President.E2.80.99s_Desk_Dal_Sanders_Page_8-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Society of American Magicians, at their National Council Meeting in Boca Raton, Florida, in 2013, under the prompting of The Houdini Museum's Dorothy Dietrich and Dick Brookz, voted to assume the financial responsibilities for the care and maintenance of the Houdini Gravesite. In MUM Magazine, the Society's official magazine, President Dal Sanders announced "Harry Houdini is an icon as revered as Elvis Presley or Marilyn Monroe. He is not only a magical icon; his gravesite bears the seal of The Society of American Magicians. That seal is our brand and we should be proud to protect it. This gravesite is clearly our responsibility and Im proud to report that the National Council unanimously voted to maintain Houdinis final resting place."
     </p>
     <p>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abracadabra:_Houdini.E2.80.99s_grave_to_get_a_facelift_79-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Abracadabra:_Houdini.E2.80.99s_grave_to_get_a_facelift-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Houdini Gravesite Restoration Committee under the Chairmanship of National President-Elect David Bowers, is working closely with National President Kenrick "Ice" McDonald to see this project to completion. Bowers said it is a foregone conclusion that the Society will approve the funding request, because Houdini is responsible for the Society of American Magicians being what it is today. We owe a debt of gratitude to him. Like Bowers, McDonald said the motivation behind the repairs is to properly honor the grave of the Babe Ruth of magicians. This is hallowed ground, he said. When you ask people about magicians, the first thing they say is Harry Houdini. While the actual plot will remain under the control of Machpelah Cemetery management, the Society of American Magicians, with the help of the Houdini Museum in Pennsylvania, will be in charge of the restoration.
     </p>
     <p>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houdini.27s_gravesite_to_get_a_magic_fix_in_Queens_80-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Houdini.27s_gravesite_to_get_a_magic_fix_in_Queens-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Magicians Dorothy Dietrich and Dick Brookz have been caring for the escape artists Queens grave over the years. This is a monument where people go and visit on a daily basis, said Dietrich who is spearheading restoration efforts. "The nearly 80-year-old popular plot at the Machpelah Cemetery has fallen into disrepair over the years." "The Houdini Museum has teamed with The Society of American Magicians, one of the oldest fraternal magic organizations in the world, to give the beloved site a facelift." The organization has a specific Houdini gravesite committee made up of nine members headed up by President elect David Bowers who brought this project to the Societys attention. Kenrick Ice McDonald, the current president of the Society of American Magicians said You have to know the history. Houdini served as President from 1917 until his death in 1926. Houdinis burial site needs an infusion of cash to restore it to its former glory." Magician Dietrich said the repairs could cost tens of thousands of dollars, after consulting with glass experts and grave artisans. Its a wonderful project, but its taken a lifetime to get people interested, she said. Its long overdue, and its great that its happening. Houdini was a living superhero, Dietrich said. He wasnt just a magician and escape artist, he was great humanitarian.
     </p>
     <p>
      To this day the Society holds a
      <a href="/wiki/Broken_wand_ceremony" title="Broken wand ceremony">
       broken wand ceremony
      </a>
      at the grave every November. Houdini's widow,
      <a href="/wiki/Bess_Houdini" title="Bess Houdini">
       Bess
      </a>
      , died of a heart attack on February 11, 1943, aged 67, in
      <a href="/wiki/Needles,_California" title="Needles, California">
       Needles, California
      </a>
      while on a train en route from Los Angeles to New York City. She had expressed a wish to be buried next to her husband, but instead was interred 35miles due north at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gate_of_Heaven_Cemetery" title="Gate of Heaven Cemetery">
       Gate of Heaven Cemetery
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Westchester_County,_New_York" title="Westchester County, New York">
       Westchester County, New York
      </a>
      , as her Catholic family refused to allow her to be buried in a Jewish cemetery.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tmulti tnone center">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:608px;max-width:608px">
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Houdini_Gravesite_1024.jpg">
          <img alt="The gravesite of Harry Houdini" data-file-height="685" data-file-width="1024" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Houdini_Gravesite_1024.jpg/300px-Houdini_Gravesite_1024.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Houdini_Gravesite_1024.jpg/450px-Houdini_Gravesite_1024.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Houdini_Gravesite_1024.jpg/600px-Houdini_Gravesite_1024.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         The gravesite of Harry Houdini
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Harry_Houdini_Grave_Marker_8-2008.jpg">
          <img alt="The grave marker at Harry Houdini's burial site" data-file-height="685" data-file-width="1024" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Harry_Houdini_Grave_Marker_8-2008.jpg/300px-Harry_Houdini_Grave_Marker_8-2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Harry_Houdini_Grave_Marker_8-2008.jpg/450px-Harry_Houdini_Grave_Marker_8-2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Harry_Houdini_Grave_Marker_8-2008.jpg/600px-Harry_Houdini_Grave_Marker_8-2008.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         The grave marker at Harry Houdini's burial site
        </div>
       </div>
       <div style="clear:left">
       </div>
       <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">
        Weiss Family Grave Memorial Site at
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Machpelah_Cemetery_(Queens,_New_York)" title="Machpelah Cemetery (Queens, New York)">
         Machpelah Cemetery
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_exhumation">
       Proposed exhumation
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On March 22, 2007, Houdini's grand-nephew (the grandson of his brother Theo), George Hardeen, announced that the courts would be asked to allow
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exhumation" title="Exhumation">
       exhumation
      </a>
      of Houdini's body, to investigate the possibility of Houdini being murdered by spiritualists, as suggested in the biography
      <i>
       The Secret Life of Houdini
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In a statement given to the
      <a href="/wiki/Houdini_Museum" title="Houdini Museum">
       Houdini Museum
      </a>
      in Scranton, the family of Bess Houdini opposed the application and suggested it was a publicity ploy for the book.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">
        The Washington Post
       </a>
      </i>
      stated that the press conference was not arranged by the family of Houdini. Instead, the
      <i>
       Post
      </i>
      reported, it was orchestrated by authors Kalush and Sloman, who hired the PR firm Dan Klores Communications to promote their book.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2008, it was revealed the parties involved never filed legal papers to perform an exhumation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">
       Legacy
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Houdini's brother,
      <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Hardeen" title="Theodore Hardeen">
       Theodore Hardeen
      </a>
      , who returned to performing after Houdini's death, inherited his brother's effects and props. Houdini's will stipulated that all the effects should be "burned and destroyed" upon Hardeen's death. Hardeen sold much of the collection to magician and Houdini enthusiast
      <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Hollis_Radner" title="Sidney Hollis Radner">
       Sidney Hollis Radner
      </a>
      during the 1940s, including the water torture cell.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Radner allowed choice pieces of the collection to be displayed at The Houdini Magical Hall of Fame in
      <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls,_Ontario" title="Niagara Falls, Ontario">
       Niagara Falls, Ontario
      </a>
      . In 1995, a fire destroyed the museum. The water torture cell's metal frame remained, and it was restored by illusion builder John Gaughan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many of the props contained in the museum such as the mirror handcuffs, Houdini's original packing crate, a milk can, and a straitjacket, survived the fire and were auctioned off in 1999 and 2008.
     </p>
     <p>
      Radner loaned the bulk of his collection for archiving to the Outagamie Museum in Appleton, Wisconsin; but pulled it in 2003, and auctioned
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-houdini_88-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-houdini-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      it off a year later in Las Vegas, on October 30, 2004.
     </p>
     <p>
      Houdini was a "formidable collector," and bequeathed many of his holdings and paper archives on magic and spiritualism to the
      <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">
       Library of Congress
      </a>
      , which became the basis for the Houdini collection in cyberspace.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Higbee_89-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Higbee-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      More than half of Houdini's archival estate holdings and memorabilia were willed to his fellow magician and friend, John Mulholland (18971970). In 1991, illusionist and television performer
      <a href="/wiki/David_Copperfield_(illusionist)" title="David Copperfield (illusionist)">
       David Copperfield
      </a>
      purchased all of Mulholland's Houdini holdings from Mulholland's estate. These are now archived and preserved in Copperfield's warehouse at his headquarters in Las Vegas. It contains the world's largest collection of Houdini memorabilia, and preserves approximately 80,000 items of memorabilia of Houdini and other magicians, including Houdini's stage props and material, his rebuilt water torture cabinet and his metamorphosis trunk. It is not open to the public, but tours are available by invitation to magicians, scholars, researchers, journalists and serious collectors.
     </p>
     <p>
      In a posthumous ceremony on October 31, 1975, he was given a star on the
      <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">
       Hollywood Walk of Fame
      </a>
      at 7001 Hollywood Blvd.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      There is a
      <a href="/wiki/Houdini_Museum" title="Houdini Museum">
       Houdini Museum
      </a>
      in Scranton, Pennsylvania, billed as "the only building in the world entirely dedicated to Houdini". It is open to the public year round by reservation. It includes Houdini films, a guided tour about Houdini's life and a stage magic show. It was opened in 1991 by magicians Dorothy Dietrich and Dick Brookz.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Castle" title="The Magic Castle">
       The Magic Castle
      </a>
      , a nightclub for magicians and magic enthusiasts, as well as the clubhouse for the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_of_Magical_Arts" title="Academy of Magical Arts">
       Academy of Magical Arts
      </a>
      , features Houdini sances performed by magician
      <a href="/wiki/Misty_Lee" title="Misty Lee">
       Misty Lee
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Publications">
       Publications
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Houdini published numerous books during his career (some of which were written by his good friend
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walter_Brown_Gibson" title="Walter Brown Gibson">
       Walter Brown Gibson
      </a>
      , the creator of
      <a href="/wiki/The_Shadow" title="The Shadow">
       The Shadow
      </a>
      ):
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <i>
        The Right Way to Do Wrong: An Expos of Successful Criminals
       </i>
       (1906)
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Handcuff Secrets
       </i>
       (1907)
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        The Unmasking of Robert-Houdin
       </i>
       (1908), a debunking study of
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Eug%C3%A8ne_Robert-Houdin" title="Jean Eugne Robert-Houdin">
        Robert-Houdin
       </a>
       s alleged abilities.
      </li>
      <li>
       "Conjuring" article for the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encyclopaedia_Britannica" title="Encyclopaedia Britannica">
        Encyclopaedia Britannica
       </a>
       's 13th edition
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Magical Rope Ties and Escapes
       </i>
       (1920)
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Miracle Mongers and Their Methods
       </i>
       (1920)
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Houdini's Paper Magic
       </i>
       (1921)
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        A Magician Among the Spirits
       </i>
       (1924)
      </li>
      <li>
       "
       <a href="/wiki/Imprisoned_with_the_Pharaohs" title="Imprisoned with the Pharaohs">
        Imprisoned with the Pharaohs
       </a>
       " (1924), a short story ghost written by
       <a href="/wiki/H._P._Lovecraft" title="H. P. Lovecraft">
        H. P. Lovecraft
       </a>
       .
      </li>
     </ul>

         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHarry+Houdini&amp;rft.btitle=Time+to+bury+the+Houdini+exhumation&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.wildabouthoudini.com%2F2010%2F11%2Ftime-to-bury-houdini-exhumation.html&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-86">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-86">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation news">
          "In Sadness, Prime Houdini Artifact Collector Puts Items on Auction Block".
          <i>
           New York Times
          </i>
          . October 29, 2004.
          <q>
           ... Mr. Radner, aka Rendar the Magician, owns one of the world's biggest and most valuable collections of Harry Houdini artifacts, including the Chinese Water Torture Cell, one of Houdini's signature props from 1912 until his death in 1926. Most of the items were given to Mr. Radner in the 1940s by Houdini's brother, Theodore Hardeen. Hardeen considered Radner, then a student at Yale with a reputation for jumping from diving boards in handcuffs, as his protg. Until early this year, the collection was on display at the Outagamie Museum in Appleton, Wisconsin, where Houdini's father was the town rabbi in the 1870s. But after a rancorous falling out between Mr. Radner and museum officials, the 1,000-piece collection was packed up and shipped here, where it will be auctioned on Saturday in the windowless back room at the Liberace Museum and on eBay.
          </q>
         </span>

       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Walter_B._Gibson" title="Walter B. Gibson">
        Walter B. Gibson
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        Prepared from Houdini's private notebooks
       </i>
       Blue Ribbon Books, Inc., 1930. Reveals some of Houdini's magic and escape methods (also released in two separate volumes:
       <i>
        Houdini's Magic
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Houdini's Escapes
       </i>
       ).
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        The Secrets of Houdini
       </i>
       by J.C. Cannell, Hutchinson &amp; Co., London, 1931. Reveals some of Houdini's escape methods.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Houdini and Conan Doyle: The Story of a Strange Friendship
       </i>
       by Bernard M. L. Ernst, Albert &amp; Charles Boni, Inc., NY, 1932.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Sixty Years of Psychical Research
       </i>
       by Joseph F. Rinn, Truth Seeker Co., 1950, Rinn was a long time close friend of Houdini. Contains detailed information about the last Houdini message (there are 3) and its disclosure.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Houdini's Fabulous Magic
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Walter_B._Gibson" title="Walter B. Gibson">
        Walter B. Gibson
       </a>
       and Morris N. Young Chilton, NY, 1960. Excellent reference for Houdini's escapes and some methods (includes the Water Torture Cell).
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        The Houdini Birth Research Committee's Report
       </i>
       , Magico Magazine (reprint of report by The Society of American Magicians), 1972. Concludes Houdini was born March 24, 1874, in Budapest.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Mediums, Mystics and the Occult
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Milbourne_Christopher" title="Milbourne Christopher">
        Milbourne Christopher
       </a>
       , Thomas T. Crowell Co., 1975, pp.122145,
       <i>
        Arthur Ford-Messages from the Dead,
       </i>
       contains detailed information about the Houdini messages and their disclosure.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Arthur Ford: The Man Who Talked with the Dead
       </i>
       by Allen Spraggett with William V. Rauscher, 1973, pp.152165, Chapter 7,
       <i>
        The Houdini Affair
       </i>
       contains detailed information about the Houdini messages and their disclosure.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Houdini: Escape into Legend, The Early Years: 18621900
       </i>
       by Manny Weltman, Finders/Seekers Enterprises, Los Angeles, 1993. Examination of Houdini's childhood and early career.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Houdini Comes To America
       </i>
       by Ronald J. Hilgert, The Houdini Historical Center, 1996. Documents the Weiss family's immigration to the United States on July 3, 1878 (when Ehrich was 4).
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Houdini Unlocked
       </i>
       by Patrick Culliton, Two volume box set:
       <i>
        The Tao of Houdini
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        The Secret Confessions of Houdini
       </i>
       , Kieran Press, 1997.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        The Houdini Code Mystery: A Spirit Secret Solved
       </i>
       by William V. Rauscher, Magic Words, 2000.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Final Sance. The Strange Friendship Between Houdini and Conan Doyle
       </i>
       by Massimo Polidoro, Prometheus Books, 2001.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        The Man Who Killed Houdini
       </i>
       by Don Bell, Vehicle Press, 2004. Investigates J. Gordon Whitehead and the events surrounding Houdini's death.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Disappearing Tricks: Silent Film, Houdini, and the New Magic of the Twentieth Century
       </i>
       by Matthew Solomon,
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_Press" title="University of Illinois Press">
        University of Illinois Press
       </a>
       , 2010. Contains new information about Houdini's early movie career.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Houdini Art and Magic
       </i>
       by Brooke Kamin Rapaport, Jewish Museum, 2010. Essays on Houdini's life and work are accompanied by interviews with novelist E.L. Doctorow, Teller, Kenneth Silverman, and more.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Houdini The Key
       </i>
       by Patrick Culliton, Kieran Press, 2010. Reveals the authentic working methods of many of Houdini effects, including the Milk Can and Water Torture Cell. Limited to 278 copies.
      </li>
     </ul>
